MigrationLoader:\n22:     \"\"\"\n23:     Load migration files from disk and their status from the database.\n24: \n25:     Migration files are expected to live in the \"migrations\" directory of\n26:     an app. Their names are entirely unimportant from a code perspective,\n27:     but will probably follow the 1234_name.py convention.\n28: \n29:     On initialization, this class will scan those There are\\n69:     no implicit dependencies between numbered migrations - the numbering is\\n70:     merely a convention to aid file listing. Every new numbered migration\\n71:     has a declared dependency to the previous number, meaning that VCS\\n72:     branch merges can be detected and resolved.\\n73: \\n74:     Migrations files can be marked as replacing another set of migrations -\\n75:     this is to support the \\\"squash\\\" feature. The graph handler isn't\\n76:     responsible for these; instead, the code to load them in here should\\n77:     examine the migration files and if the replaced migrations are all either\\n78:     unapplied or not present, it should ignore the replaced ones, load in just\\n79:     the replacing migration, and repoint any dependencies that pointed to the\\n80:     replaced migrations to point to the replacing one.\\n81: \\n82:     A node should be a tuple: (app_path, migration_name). The tree\\n83:     special-cases things within an app - namely, root nodes and leaf nodes\\n84:     ignore dependencies to other apps.\\n85:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n86: \\n87:     def __init__(self):\\n88:         self.node_map = {}\\n89:         self.nodes = {}\\n90: \\n91:     def add_node(self, key, migration):\\n92:         assert key not in self.node_map\\n93:         node = Node(key)\\n94:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n95:         self.nodes[key] = migration\\n96: \\n97:     def add_dummy_node(self, key, origin, error_message):\\n98:         node = DummyNode(key, origin, error_message)\\n99:         self.node_map[key] = node\\n100:         self.nodes[key] = None\\n101: \\n102:     def add_dependency(self, migration, child, parent, skip_validation=False):\\n103:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n104:         This may create dummy nodes if they don't yet exist. Any\\n128:         dependencies that were referencing them are changed to reference the\\n129:         `replacement` node instead.\\n130:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n131:         # Cast list of replaced keys to set to speed up lookup later.\\n132:         replaced = set(replaced)\\n133:         try:\\n134:             replacement_node = self.node_map[replacement]\\n135:         except KeyError as err:\\n136:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n137:                 \\\"Unable to find replacement node %r. It was either never added\\\"\\n138:                 \\\" to the migration graph, or has been removed.\\\" % (replacement,),\\n139:                 replacement,\\n140:             ) from err\\n141:         for replaced_key in replaced:\\n142:             self.nodes.pop(replaced_key, None)\\n143:             replaced_node = self.node_map.pop(replaced_key, None)\\n144:             if replaced_node:\\n145:                 for child in replaced_node.children:\\n146:                     child.parents.remove(replaced_node)\\n147:                     # We don't want to create dependencies between the replaced\\n148:                     # node and the replacement node as this would lead to\\n149:                     # self-referencing on the replacement node at a later\\n150:                     # iteration.\\n151:                     if child.key not in replaced:\\n152:                         replacement_node.add_child(child)\\n153:                         child.add_parent(replacement_node)\\n154:                 for parent in replaced_node.parents:\\n155:                     parent.children.remove(replaced_node)\\n156:                     # Again, to avoid self-referencing.\\n157:                     if parent.key not in replaced:\\n158:                         replacement_node.add_parent(parent)\\n159:                         parent.add_child(replacement_node)\\n160: \\n161:     def remove_replacement_node(self, replacement, replaced):\\n162:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n163:         The inverse operation to `remove_replaced_nodes`. Almost. Remove the\\n164:         replacement node `replacement` and remap its child nodes to `replaced`\\n165:         - the list of nodes it would have replaced. Don't remap its parent\\n166:         nodes as they are expected to be correct already.\\n167:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n168:         self.nodes.pop(replacement, None)\\n169:         try:\\n170:             replacement_node = self.node_map.pop(replacement)\\n171:         except KeyError as err:\\n172:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n173:                 \\\"Unable to remove replacement node %r. compliance system is implemented across seven core modules in the django/db/migrations package, along with the squashmigrations management command.\\n\\n**Squash Migration Generator** (django/core/management/commands/squashmigrations.py:Command.handle)\\nThe `Command` class in squashmigrations.py is the primary entry point for generating squashed migrations. It loads all migrations to be squashed, extracts their operations and dependencies, applies optimization if requested, and creates a new Migration subclass with the `replaces` attribute set to list all replaced migration keys. When migrations with missing dependencies are encountered, DummyNode instances are created as placeholders. After replacements are processed, this method checks that all such dummy nodes have been replaced, otherwise raising NodeNotFoundError\\n- django/db/migrations/graph.py (MigrationGraph.ensure_not_cyclic(), lines 271-294): Performs cycle detection using a depth-first search algorithm to prevent circular dependency chains from being introduced during squashing\\n- django/db/migrations/graph.py (MigrationGraph.remove_replaced_nodes(), lines 125-159): When a squash migration replaces others, this method removes the replaced nodes from the graph and remaps all dependencies that pointed to them to instead point to the replacement node\\n- django/db/migrations/graph.py (MigrationGraph.remove_replacement_node(), lines 161-196): The inverse operation - handles the case where a replacement migration cannot be used (e.g., when only partially applied) by removing it and remapping children back to the replaced nodes\\n- django/db/migrations/loader.py (MigrationLoader.build_graph(), lines 274-342): Orchestrates the entire graph building process, calling validate_consistency() after all replacements are processed (line 313) and ensure_not_cyclic() afterward (line 342)\\n\\n**Squash Completeness Check** validates that squashed migrations are properly applied:\\n- django/db/migrations/executor.py (MigrationExecutor.check_replacements(), lines 294-308): Called after every migration execution to mark replacement migrations as applied when all of their replaced migrations have been applied. This handles the case where a new squash migration is deployed to a system that already had all its replaced migrations applied\\n- django/db/migrations/executor.py (MigrationExecutor.record_migration(), lines 268-277): When a replacement migration is applied, this method recursively records the applied status of all individual replaced migrations in the database\\n- django/db/migrations/loader.py (MigrationLoader.all_replaced_applied(), lines 372-384): Recursively checks whether all migrations that a squash migration replaces are in the applied set, handling nested squashed migrations\\n- django/db/migrations/loader.py (MigrationLoader._resolve_replaced_migration_keys(), lines 224-233): Recursively resolves the complete set of replaced migrations, accounting for squashed migrations that themselves replace other squashed migrations\\n- django/db/migrations/loader.py (MigrationLoader.replace_migration(), lines 235-272): Orchestrates the replacement process by determining whether the replacement migration can be used (all or none of replaced migrations applied) versus partial application scenarios that require different graph handling\\n- django/db/migrations/loader.py (MigrationLoader.check_consistent_history(), lines 344-370): Validates that no applied migration has unapplied dependencies, with special handling for squashed migrations to allow unapplied squashes if all their replaced migrations are applied\\n\\nThe system ensures that squash migrations are transparent to the database while maintaining complete dependency tracking and validation across all migration states.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
